<h2 id=358 pos="bottom right">Iterables</h2>
<p id=359 pos="bottom right">When you create a list, you can read its items one by one. Reading its items one by one is called iteration:</p>
<span id=362 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>
<span id=363 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=364 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">2</span>
<span id=365 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">3</span>
<span id=366 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>
<span id=367 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">for</span>
<span id=368 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">in</span>
<span id=369 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">...</span>
<span id=370 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">print</span>
<span id=371 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=372 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">2</span>
<span id=373 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">3</span>
<code id=375 pos="bottom right">mylist</code>
<em id=376 pos="bottom right">iterable</em>
<span id=379 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>

<span id=383 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">3</span>

<span id=391 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">4</span>
<code id=393 pos="bottom right">for... in...</code>
<code id=394 pos="bottom right">lists</code>
<code id=395 pos="bottom right">strings</code>
<p id=396 pos="bottom right">These iterables are handy because you can read them as much as you wish, but you store all the values in memory and this is not always what you want when you have a lot of values.</p>
<h2 id=397 pos="bottom right">Generators</h2>

<p id=455 pos="bottom right">Here it's a useless example, but it's handy when you know your function will return a huge set of values that you will only need to read once.</p>
<code id=457 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<strong id=458 pos="bottom right">when you call the function, the code you have written in the function body does not run.</strong>
<code id=460 pos="bottom right">for</code>

<code id=463 pos="bottom right">for</code>
<code id=464 pos="bottom right">yield</code>

<code id=466 pos="bottom right">"if/else"</code>

<h2 id=468 pos="bottom right">Your code explained</h2>
<em id=470 pos="bottom right">Generator:</em>
<span id=473 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># Here you create the method of the node object that will return the generator</span>
<span id=474 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=475 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">_get_child_candidates</span>
<span id=476 class="hljs-params" pos="bottom right">self, distance, min_dist, max_dist</span>
<span id=477 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># Here is the code that will be called each time you use the generator object:</span>
<span id=478 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># If there is still a child of the node object on its left</span>
<span id=479 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># AND if the distance is ok, return the next child</span>
<span id=480 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">if</span>
<span id=481 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">and</span>
<span id=482 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">yield</span>
<span id=483 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># If there is still a child of the node object on its right</span>
<span id=484 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># AND if the distance is ok, return the next child</span>
<span id=485 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">if</span>
<span id=486 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">and</span>
<span id=487 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">yield</span>
<span id=488 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># If the function arrives here, the generator will be considered empty</span>
<span id=489 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># There are no more than two values: the left and the right children</span>
<em id=491 pos="bottom right">Caller:</em>
<span id=494 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># Create an empty list and a list with the current object reference</span>
<span id=495 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">list</span>
<span id=496 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># Loop on candidates (they contain only one element at the beginning)</span>
<span id=497 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">while</span>
<span id=498 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># Get the last candidate and remove it from the list</span>
<span id=499 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># Get the distance between obj and the candidate</span>
<span id=500 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># If the distance is ok, then you can fill in the result</span>
<span id=501 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">if</span>
<span id=502 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">and</span>
<span id=503 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># Add the children of the candidate to the candidate's list</span>
<span id=504 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># so the loop will keep running until it has looked</span>
<span id=505 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># at all the children of the children of the children, etc. of the candidate</span>
<span id=506 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">return</span>
<p id=507 pos="bottom right">This code contains several smart parts:</p>
<code id=511 pos="bottom right">candidates.extend(node._get_child_candidates(distance, min_dist, max_dist))</code>
<code id=512 pos="bottom right">while</code>
<code id=515 pos="bottom right">extend()</code>
<p id=516 pos="bottom right">Usually, we pass a list to it:</p>

<span id=530 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">3</span>
<span id=531 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">4</span>
<p id=532 pos="bottom right">But in your code, it gets a generator, which is good because:</p>
<li id=534 pos="bottom right">You don't need to read the values twice.</li>
<li id=535 pos="bottom right">You may have a lot of children and you don't want them all stored in memory.</li>
<p id=536 pos="bottom right">And it works because Python does not care if the argument of a method is a list or not. Python expects iterables so it will work with strings, lists, tuples, and generators! This is called duck typing and is one of the reasons why Python is so cool. But this is another story, for another question...</p>
<p id=537 pos="bottom right">You can stop here, or read a little bit to see an advanced use of a generator:</p>

<h2 id=853 pos="bottom right">Don't confuse your iterables, iterators, and generators</h2>
<strong id=855 pos="bottom right">iterator protocol</strong>
<span id=858 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">for</span>
<span id=859 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">in</span>
<p id=860 pos="bottom right">Python performs the following two steps:</p>
<code id=864 pos="bottom right">mylist</code>
<code id=866 pos="bottom right">iter(mylist)</code>
<code id=867 pos="bottom right">next()</code>
<code id=868 pos="bottom right">__next__()</code>
<p id=869 pos="bottom right">[This is the step most people forget to tell you about]</p>
<p id=871 pos="bottom right">Uses the iterator to loop over items:</p>
<code id=873 pos="bottom right">next()</code>
<code id=874 pos="bottom right">next()</code>
<code id=875 pos="bottom right">x</code>
<code id=876 pos="bottom right">StopIteration</code>
<code id=877 pos="bottom right">next()</code>
<em id=879 pos="bottom right">loop over</em>
<code id=880 pos="bottom right">otherlist.extend(mylist)</code>
<code id=881 pos="bottom right">otherlist</code>
<code id=883 pos="bottom right">mylist</code>
<em id=884 pos="bottom right">iterable</em>
<code id=885 pos="bottom right">__iter__()</code>
<em id=886 pos="bottom right">iterator</em>
<code id=887 pos="bottom right">next()</code>
<code id=888 pos="bottom right">__iter__()</code>
<code id=889 pos="bottom right">next()</code>
<code id=890 pos="bottom right">__iter__()</code>
<code id=891 pos="bottom right">self</code>
<p id=892 pos="bottom right">So that's the iterator protocol, many objects implement this protocol:</p>
<li id=894 pos="bottom right">Built-in lists, dictionaries, tuples, sets, and files.</li>
<code id=896 pos="bottom right">__iter__()</code>
<li id=897 pos="bottom right">Generators.</li>
<code id=899 pos="bottom right">for</code>
<code id=900 pos="bottom right">next()</code>
<em id=901 pos="bottom right">keys</em>
<em id=902 pos="bottom right">lines</em>
<code id=903 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<span id=906 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>

<p id=1027 pos="bottom right">Original version:</p>
<span id=1030 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=1031 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">some_function</span>
<span id=1032 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">for</span>

<p id=1039 pos="bottom right">This is basically what the Python interpreter does with the above code:</p>
<span id=1042 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">class</span>
<span id=1043 class="hljs-title class_" pos="bottom right">it</span>
<span id=1044 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=1045 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">__init__</span>
<span id=1046 class="hljs-params" pos="bottom right">self</span>
<span id=1047 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># Start at -1 so that we get 0 when we add 1 below.</span>
<span id=1048 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=1049 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># The __iter__ method will be called once by the 'for' loop.</span>
<span id=1050 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># The rest of the magic happens on the object returned by this method.</span>
<span id=1051 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># In this case it is the object itself.</span>
<span id=1052 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=1053 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">__iter__</span>
<span id=1054 class="hljs-params" pos="bottom right">self</span>
<span id=1055 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">return</span>
<span id=1056 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># The next method will be called repeatedly by the 'for' loop</span>
<span id=1057 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># until it raises StopIteration.</span>
<span id=1058 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=1059 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">next</span>
<span id=1060 class="hljs-params" pos="bottom right">self</span>

<span id=1063 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">4</span>
<span id=1064 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">return</span>
<span id=1065 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">else</span>
<span id=1066 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># A StopIteration exception is raised</span>
<span id=1067 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># to signal that the iterator is done.</span>
<span id=1068 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># This is caught implicitly by the 'for' loop.</span>

<code id=1178 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<code id=1181 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<em id=1182 pos="bottom right">anywhere</em>
<code id=1183 pos="bottom right">return</code>
<strong id=1185 pos="bottom right">Instead</strong>
<strong id=1186 pos="bottom right">immediately</strong>
<strong id=1187 pos="bottom right">lazy "pending list" object</strong>
<em id=1189 pos="bottom right">iterable</em>
<code id=1190 pos="bottom right">list</code>
<code id=1191 pos="bottom right">set</code>
<code id=1192 pos="bottom right">range</code>
<em id=1193 pos="bottom right">built-in protocol for visiting each element in a certain order</em>
<strong id=1195 pos="bottom right">a generator is a lazy, incrementally-pending list</strong>
<code id=1197 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<strong id=1198 pos="bottom right">Furthermore, advanced usage lets you use generators as coroutines (see below).</strong>
<span id=1201 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># basically a list (but lazy)</span>
<span id=1202 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">list</span>
<span id=1203 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># evaluate every element into a list</span>
<span id=1204 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">0</span>
<span id=1205 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">0</span>
<span id=1206 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=1207 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">0</span>
<span id=1208 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=1209 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">2</span>
<span id=1210 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">0</span>
<span id=1211 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=1212 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">2</span>
<code id=1214 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<code id=1215 pos="bottom right">next()</code>

<h2 id=1251 pos="bottom right">Comparing the example to "just returning a list"</h2>
<p id=1252 pos="bottom right">The above example can be thought of as merely creating a list that you append to and return:</p>
<span id=1255 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># return a list                  #  # return a generator</span>
<span id=1256 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=1257 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">makeRange</span>
<span id=1258 class="hljs-params" pos="bottom right">n</span>
<span id=1259 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right">#  def makeRange(n):</span>
<span id=1260 class="hljs-string" pos="bottom right">"""return [0,1,2,...,n-1]"""</span>
<span id=1261 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right">#      """return 0,1,2,...,n-1"""</span>
<span id=1262 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right">#</span>
<span id=1263 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">0</span>
<span id=1264 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right">#      i = 0</span>
<span id=1265 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">while</span>
<span id=1266 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right">#      while i < n:</span>
<span id=1267 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right">#          yield i</span>
<span id=1268 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=1269 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right">#          i += 1</span>
<span id=1270 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">return</span>
<span id=1271 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right">#</span>
<span id=1272 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>
<span id=1273 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">5</span>
<span id=1274 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">0</span>
<span id=1275 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=1276 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">2</span>
<span id=1277 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">3</span>
<span id=1278 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">4</span>
<p id=1279 pos="bottom right">There is one major difference, though; see the last section.</p>
<hr id=1280 pos="bottom right"></hr>
<h2 id=1281 pos="bottom right">How you might use generators</h2>
<p id=1282 pos="bottom right">An iterable is the last part of a list comprehension, and all generators are iterable, so they're often used like so:</p>
<span id=1285 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right">#                  < ITERABLE ></span>
<span id=1286 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>
<span id=1287 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">10</span>
<span id=1288 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">for</span>
<span id=1289 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">in</span>
<span id=1290 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">5</span>
<span id=1291 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">10</span>
<span id=1292 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">11</span>
<span id=1293 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">12</span>
<span id=1294 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">13</span>
<span id=1295 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">14</span>
<code id=1297 pos="bottom right">itertools</code>

<code id=1299 pos="bottom right">chain</code>
<code id=1300 pos="bottom right">itertools.count()</code>
<code id=1301 pos="bottom right">def enumerate(iterable): zip(count(), iterable)</code>
<code id=1302 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<a id=1304 pos="bottom right">implementing coroutines</a>

<hr id=1340 pos="bottom right"></hr>
<h2 id=1341 pos="bottom right">Coroutines</h2>
<a id=1343 pos="bottom right">Coroutine</a>
<span id=1346 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=1347 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">interactiveProcedure</span>
<span id=1348 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">yield</span>
<span id=1349 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">print</span>
<span id=1350 class="hljs-string" pos="bottom right">'user response:'</span>
<span id=1351 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">yield</span>
<span id=1352 class="hljs-string" pos="bottom right">'success'</span>
<span id=1353 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">next</span>
<span id=1354 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># same as .send(None)</span>
<span id=1355 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># ...at some point later on web form submit...</span>
<code id=1357 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<code id=1358 pos="bottom right">nextInput = yield nextOutput</code>
<code id=1359 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<code id=1360 pos="bottom right">next</code>
<strong id=1362 pos="bottom right">You can think of Python coroutines as lazy incrementally-pending lists, where the next element doesn't just depend on the previous computation but also on input that you may opt to inject during the generation process.</strong>
<hr id=1363 pos="bottom right"></hr>
<h2 id=1364 pos="bottom right">Minutiae</h2>
<p id=1365 pos="bottom right">Normally, most people would not care about the following distinctions and probably want to stop reading here.</p>
<em id=1367 pos="bottom right">iterable</em>
<code id=1368 pos="bottom right">[1,2,3]</code>
<em id=1369 pos="bottom right">iterator</em>
<code id=1370 pos="bottom right">[1,2,3].__iter__()</code>
<em id=1371 pos="bottom right">generator</em>
<p id=1372 pos="bottom right">When you request an iterator from a list, it creates a new iterator. However, when you request an iterator from an iterator (which you would rarely do), it just gives you a copy of itself.</p>
<p id=1373 pos="bottom right">Thus, in the unlikely event that you are failing to do something like this...</p>
<span id=1376 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">5</span>
<span id=1377 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">list</span>
<span id=1378 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">0</span>
<span id=1379 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=1380 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">2</span>
<span id=1381 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">3</span>
<span id=1382 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">4</span>
<span id=1383 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">list</span>
<em id=1385 pos="bottom right">iterator</em>
<code id=1386 pos="bottom right">myRange(...)</code>
<code id=1387 pos="bottom right">x = list(myRange(5))</code>
<code id=1389 pos="bottom right">itertools.tee</code>
<a id=1390 pos="bottom right">still works in Python 3</a>
<a id=1391 pos="bottom right">copyable iterator Python PEP standards proposal</a>

<h1 id=1500 pos="bottom right">Generators:</h1>
<code id=1503 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<code id=1505 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<a id=1507 pos="bottom right">frozen</a>
<code id=1509 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<a id=1510 pos="bottom right">implementing the iterator protocol</a>
<code id=1511 pos="bottom right">__iter__</code>
<code id=1512 pos="bottom right">__next__</code>

<p id=1523 pos="bottom right">Let's do some introspection:</p>

<span id=1531 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>

<span id=1537 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>

<span id=1542 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>

<span id=1546 class="hljs-literal" pos="bottom right">True</span>

<p id=1548 pos="bottom right">The generator type is a sub-type of iterator:</p>

<span id=1557 class="hljs-literal" pos="bottom right">True</span>
<p id=1558 pos="bottom right">And if necessary, we can type-check like this:</p>
<span id=1561 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>
<span id=1562 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">isinstance</span>
<span id=1563 class="hljs-literal" pos="bottom right">True</span>

<a id=1569 pos="bottom right">is that once exhausted</a>
<span id=1572 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>
<span id=1573 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">list</span>
<span id=1574 class="hljs-string" pos="bottom right">'I am'</span>
<span id=1575 class="hljs-string" pos="bottom right">'a generator!'</span>
<span id=1576 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>

<p id=1578 pos="bottom right">You'll have to make another if you want to use its functionality again (see footnote 2):</p>
<span id=1581 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>

<span id=1583 class="hljs-string" pos="bottom right">'I am'</span>

<h2 id=1723 pos="bottom right">Critique of the Top/Accepted Answer**</h2>
<strong id=1726 pos="bottom right">iterable</strong>
<strong id=1727 pos="bottom right">iterable</strong>
<code id=1728 pos="bottom right">__iter__</code>
<strong id=1729 pos="bottom right">iterator</strong>
<strong id=1730 pos="bottom right">iterator</strong>
<code id=1731 pos="bottom right">.__next__</code>
<code id=1732 pos="bottom right">for</code>
<code id=1733 pos="bottom right">StopIteration</code>
<code id=1734 pos="bottom right">StopIteration</code>
<strong id=1736 pos="bottom right">iterator</strong>
<code id=1737 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<strong id=1739 pos="bottom right">Controlling a generator exhaustion</strong>
<code id=1740 pos="bottom right">.next</code>
<code id=1741 pos="bottom right">next</code>
<code id=1742 pos="bottom right">next(obj)</code>
<code id=1744 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<code id=1746 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<code id=1747 pos="bottom right">yield from</code>
<strong id=1749 pos="bottom right">The top/accepted answer is a very incomplete answer.</strong>
<code id=1751 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<p id=1752 pos="bottom right">The grammar currently allows any expression in a list comprehension.</p>
<span id=1755 class="hljs-string" pos="bottom right">'='</span>
<span id=1756 class="hljs-string" pos="bottom right">'yield'</span>
<span id=1757 class="hljs-string" pos="bottom right">'from'</span>
<p id=1758 pos="bottom right">Since yield is an expression, it has been touted by some as interesting to use it in comprehensions or generator expression - in spite of citing no particularly good use-case.</p>
<a id=1760 pos="bottom right">discussing deprecating its allowance</a>
<p id=1762 pos="bottom right">On 30 January 2017 at 19:05, Brett Cannon  wrote:</p>
<p id=1764 pos="bottom right">On Sun, 29 Jan 2017 at 16:39 Craig Rodrigues  wrote:</p>
<p id=1766 pos="bottom right">I'm OK with either approach.  Leaving things the way they are in Python 3
is no good, IMHO.</p>
<p id=1767 pos="bottom right">My vote is it be a SyntaxError since you're not getting what you expect from
the syntax.</p>
<p id=1768 pos="bottom right">I'd agree that's a sensible place for us to end up, as any code
relying on the current behaviour is really too clever to be
maintainable.</p>
<p id=1769 pos="bottom right">In terms of getting there, we'll likely want:</p>
<li id=1771 pos="bottom right">SyntaxWarning or DeprecationWarning in 3.7</li>
<li id=1772 pos="bottom right">Py3k warning in 2.7.x</li>
<li id=1773 pos="bottom right">SyntaxError in 3.8</li>
<p id=1774 pos="bottom right">Cheers, Nick.</p>

<strong id=1909 pos="bottom right">the stack frame is not cleaned up when a yield occurs, however control is transferred back to the caller, so its state will resume the next time the function is called.</strong>

<path id=1994 class="SVG_CLASS" pos="bottom right"></path>
<path id=1997 class="SVG_CLASS" pos="bottom right"></path>
<p id=2000 pos="bottom right">There's one extra thing to mention: a function that yields doesn't actually have to terminate. I've written code like this:</p>
<span id=2003 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=2004 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">fib</span>
<span id=2005 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">0</span>
<span id=2006 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=2007 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">while</span>
<span id=2008 class="hljs-literal" pos="bottom right">True</span>
<span id=2009 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">yield</span>
<p id=2010 pos="bottom right">Then I can use it in other code like this:</p>
<span id=2013 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">for</span>
<span id=2014 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">in</span>
<span id=2015 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">if</span>
<span id=2016 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">break</span>
<p id=2017 pos="bottom right">It really helps simplify some problems, and makes some things easier to work with.</p>

<strong id=2202 pos="bottom right">TL;DR</strong>
<h1 id=2203 pos="bottom right">Instead of this:</h1>
<span id=2206 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=2207 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">square_list</span>
<span id=2208 class="hljs-params" pos="bottom right">n</span>
<span id=2209 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># Replace</span>
<span id=2210 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">for</span>
<span id=2211 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">in</span>
<span id=2212 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">range</span>
<span id=2213 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># these</span>
<span id=2214 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">return</span>
<span id=2215 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># lines</span>
<h1 id=2216 pos="bottom right">do this:</h1>
<span id=2219 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=2220 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">square_yield</span>
<span id=2221 class="hljs-params" pos="bottom right">n</span>
<span id=2222 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">for</span>
<span id=2223 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">in</span>
<span id=2224 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">range</span>
<span id=2225 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">yield</span>
<span id=2226 class="hljs-comment" pos="bottom right"># with this one.</span>
<code id=2228 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<p id=2229 pos="bottom right">This was my first "aha" moment with yield.</p>
<hr id=2230 pos="bottom right"></hr>
<code id=2232 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<a id=2233 pos="bottom right">sugary</a>
<p id=2235 pos="bottom right">build a series of stuff</p>
<p id=2236 pos="bottom right">Same behavior:</p>
<span id=2239 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>
<span id=2240 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">for</span>
<span id=2241 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">in</span>
<span id=2242 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">4</span>
<span id=2243 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">...</span>
<span id=2244 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">print</span>
<span id=2245 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">0</span>
<span id=2246 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=2247 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">4</span>
<span id=2248 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">9</span>
<span id=2249 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>
<span id=2250 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">for</span>
<span id=2251 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">in</span>
<span id=2252 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">4</span>
<span id=2253 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">...</span>
<span id=2254 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">print</span>
<span id=2255 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">0</span>
<span id=2256 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=2257 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">4</span>
<span id=2258 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">9</span>
<p id=2259 pos="bottom right">Different behavior:</p>
<strong id=2261 pos="bottom right">single-pass</strong>
<a id=2262 pos="bottom right">generator function</a>
<a id=2263 pos="bottom right">iterator</a>
<strong id=2265 pos="bottom right">lazy</strong>
<em id=2266 pos="bottom right">doesn't actually execute at all when you call it.</em>
<a id=2267 pos="bottom right">iterator object</a>
<code id=2268 pos="bottom right">next()</code>
<code id=2269 pos="bottom right">return</code>
<strong id=2271 pos="bottom right">versatile</strong>
<span id=2274 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>
<span id=2275 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=2276 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">squares_all_of_them</span>
<span id=2277 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">...</span>
<span id=2278 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">0</span>
<span id=2279 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">...</span>
<span id=2280 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">while</span>
<span id=2281 class="hljs-literal" pos="bottom right">True</span>
<span id=2282 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">...</span>
<span id=2283 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">yield</span>
<span id=2284 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">...</span>
<span id=2285 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=2286 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>
<span id=2287 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>
<span id=2288 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">for</span>
<span id=2289 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">in</span>
<span id=2290 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">range</span>
<span id=2291 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">4</span>
<span id=2292 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">...</span>
<span id=2293 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">print</span>
<span id=2294 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">next</span>
<span id=2295 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">0</span>
<span id=2296 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=2297 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">4</span>
<span id=2298 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">9</span>
<hr id=2299 pos="bottom right"></hr>
<strong id=2301 pos="bottom right">multiple passes</strong>
<code id=2302 pos="bottom right">list()</code>
<span id=2305 class="hljs-meta" pos="bottom right">>>></span>
<span id=2306 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">list</span>
<span id=2307 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">4</span>
<span id=2308 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">0</span>
<span id=2309 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=2310 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">4</span>
<span id=2311 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">9</span>
<hr id=2312 pos="bottom right"></hr>
<code id=2314 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<a id=2315 pos="bottom right">both meanings</a>
<strong id=2318 pos="bottom right">yield</strong>
<p id=2319 pos="bottom right">...provide the next data in the series.</p>
<strong id=2322 pos="bottom right">yield</strong>
<p id=2323 pos="bottom right">...relinquish CPU execution until the iterator advances.</p>

<p id=2459 pos="bottom right">Yield gives you a generator.</p>
<span id=2462 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=2463 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">get_odd_numbers</span>
<span id=2464 class="hljs-params" pos="bottom right">i</span>
<span id=2465 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">return</span>
<span id=2466 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">range</span>
<span id=2467 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=2468 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">2</span>
<span id=2469 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=2470 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">yield_odd_numbers</span>
<span id=2471 class="hljs-params" pos="bottom right">i</span>
<span id=2472 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">for</span>
<span id=2473 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">in</span>
<span id=2474 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">range</span>
<span id=2475 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=2476 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">2</span>
<span id=2477 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">yield</span>
<span id=2478 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">10</span>
<span id=2479 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">10</span>
<span id=2480 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=2481 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">3</span>
<span id=2482 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">5</span>

<span id=2484 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">9</span>
<span id=2485 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">object</span>
<span id=2486 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">0x1029c6f50</span>
<span id=2487 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">next</span>
<span id=2488 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=2489 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">next</span>
<span id=2490 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">3</span>
<span id=2491 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">next</span>
<span id=2492 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">5</span>
<code id=2494 pos="bottom right">foo</code>
<code id=2496 pos="bottom right">bar</code>
<code id=2497 pos="bottom right">for</code>
<p id=2498 pos="bottom right">Again, this is a pretty contrived example, you probably would use itertools if you really wanted to count to 50 billion. :)</p>
<p id=2499 pos="bottom right">This is the most simple use case of generators. As you said, it can be used to write efficient permutations, using yield to push things up through the call stack instead of using some sort of stack variable. Generators can also be used for specialized tree traversal, and all manner of other things.</p>

<p id=2586 pos="bottom right">Here is an example in plain language. I will provide a correspondence between high-level human concepts to low-level Python concepts.</p>
<p id=2587 pos="bottom right">I want to operate on a sequence of numbers, but I don't want to bother myself with the creation of that sequence, I want only to focus on the operation I want to do. So, I do the following:</p>
<code id=2591 pos="bottom right">def</code>
<code id=2592 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<b id=2594 pos="bottom right">This step corresponds to calling the generator function which returns a generator object.</b>

<li id=2603 pos="bottom right">‚Ä¶ repeat the previous step, until‚Ä¶</li>

<p id=2713 pos="bottom right">There is one type of answer that I don't feel has been given yet, among the many great answers that describe how to use generators. Here is the programming language theory answer:</p>
<code id=2715 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<i id=2716 pos="bottom right">continuations</i>
<p id=2717 pos="bottom right">Continuations in programming languages theory are a much more fundamental kind of computation, but they are not often used, because they are extremely hard to reason about and also very difficult to implement. But the idea of what a continuation is, is straightforward: it is the state of a computation that has not yet finished. In this state, the current values of variables, the operations that have yet to be performed, and so on, are saved. Then at some point later in the program the continuation can be invoked, such that the program's variables are reset to that state and the operations that were saved are carried out.</p>
<code id=2719 pos="bottom right">call/cc</code>
<p id=2720 pos="bottom right">In continuation passing style (CPS), continuations are just normal functions (only in languages where functions are first class) which the programmer explicitly manages and passes around to subroutines. In this style, program state is represented by closures (and the variables that happen to be encoded in them) rather than variables that reside somewhere on the stack. Functions that manage control flow accept continuation as arguments (in some variations of CPS, functions may accept multiple continuations) and manipulate control flow by invoking them by simply calling them and returning afterwards. A very simple example of continuation passing style is as follows:</p>
<span id=2723 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=2724 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">save_file</span>
<span id=2725 class="hljs-params" pos="bottom right">filename</span>
<span id=2726 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=2727 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">write_file_continuation</span>
<p id=2728 pos="bottom right">In this (very simplistic) example, the programmer saves the operation of actually writing the file into a continuation (which can potentially be a very complex operation with many details to write out), and then passes that continuation (i.e, as a first-class closure) to another operator which does some more processing, and then calls it if necessary. (I use this design pattern a lot in actual GUI programming, either because it saves me lines of code or, more importantly, to manage control flow after GUI events trigger.)</p>
<p id=2729 pos="bottom right">The rest of this post will, without loss of generality, conceptualize continuations as CPS, because it is a hell of a lot easier to understand and read.</p>
<p id=2730 pos="bottom right"></p>
<em id=2733 pos="bottom right">computation</em>
<em id=2735 pos="bottom right">iterator</em>
<span id=2738 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>

<code id=2978 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<span id=2981 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">yield</span>
<span id=2982 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">from</span>
<a id=2985 pos="bottom right">PEP 380 -- Syntax for Delegating to a Subgenerator</a>
<p id=2987 pos="bottom right">A syntax is proposed for a generator to delegate part of its operations to another generator. This allows a section of code containing 'yield' to be factored out and placed in another generator. Additionally, the subgenerator is allowed to return with a value, and the value is made available to the delegating generator.</p>
<p id=2988 pos="bottom right">The new syntax also opens up some opportunities for optimisation when one generator re-yields values produced by another.</p>
<a id=2990 pos="bottom right">this</a>
<span id=2993 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">async</span>
<span id=2994 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=2995 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">new_coroutine</span>
<span id=2996 class="hljs-params" pos="bottom right">data</span>
<span id=2997 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">await</span>
<code id=2999 pos="bottom right">yield</code>

<div id=3707 class="js-vote-count flex--item d-flex fd-column ai-center fc-theme-body-font fw-bold fs-subheading py4" pos="bottom right">92</div>

<path id=3716 class="SVG_CLASS" pos="bottom right"></path>
<code id=3720 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<p id=3721 pos="bottom right">I like to think of a thread as having a stack (even when it's not implemented that way).</p>
<p id=3722 pos="bottom right">When a normal function is called, it puts its local variables on the stack, does some computation, then clears the stack and returns. The values of its local variables are never seen again.</p>
<code id=3724 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<code id=3725 pos="bottom right">next()</code>
<code id=3726 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<code id=3727 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<p id=3728 pos="bottom right">So it's a kind of a frozen function that the generator is hanging onto.</p>

<a id=4203 pos="bottom right">underlying implementation of generator mechanism</a>
<code id=4205 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<code id=4206 pos="bottom right">return</code>
<code id=4207 pos="bottom right">generator function</code>
<code id=4208 pos="bottom right">generator</code>
<code id=4210 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<strong id=4211 pos="bottom right">can be thought of</strong>
<code id=4212 pos="bottom right">StopIteration</code>
<code id=4213 pos="bottom right">generator</code>
<a id=4214 pos="bottom right">one</a>
<code id=4215 pos="bottom right">functional programming perspective</code>
<code id=4217 pos="bottom right">generator</code>
<code id=4218 pos="bottom right">iterator</code>
<em id=4220 pos="bottom right">essential motivation</em>
<em id=4222 pos="bottom right">naive</em>
<code id=4224 pos="bottom right">data</code>
<code id=4225 pos="bottom right">metadata</code>
<code id=4226 pos="bottom right">the logic how the data is computed</code>
<p id=4227 pos="bottom right">There are 2 approaches to wrap such metadata.</p>
<code id=4230 pos="bottom right">as a class</code>
<code id=4231 pos="bottom right">iterator</code>
<code id=4232 pos="bottom right">__next__()</code>
<code id=4233 pos="bottom right">__iter__()</code>
<a id=4234 pos="bottom right">iterator design pattern</a>
<code id=4236 pos="bottom right">as a function</code>
<code id=4237 pos="bottom right">generator function</code>
<code id=4238 pos="bottom right">generator object</code>
<code id=4239 pos="bottom right">IS-A</code>
<p id=4240 pos="bottom right">Either way, an iterator is created, i.e. some object that can give you the data you want. The OO approach may be a bit complex. Anyway, which one to use is up to you.</p>

two
three</code>
<p id=4328 pos="bottom right">The power comes from using the generator with a loop that calculates a sequence, the generator executes the loop stopping each time to 'yield' the next result of the calculation, in this way it calculates a list on the fly, the benefit being the memory saved for especially large calculations</p>
<code id=4330 pos="bottom right">range</code>
<span id=4333 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=4334 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">myRangeNaive</span>
<span id=4335 class="hljs-params" pos="bottom right">i</span>
<span id=4336 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">0</span>
<span id=4337 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">range</span>
<span id=4338 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">while</span>
<span id=4339 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">range</span>
<span id=4340 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=4341 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">return</span>
<span id=4342 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">range</span>
<p id=4343 pos="bottom right">and use it like this;</p>
<span id=4346 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">for</span>
<span id=4347 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">in</span>
<span id=4348 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">10</span>
<span id=4349 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">print</span>
<p id=4350 pos="bottom right">But this is inefficient because</p>
<li id=4352 pos="bottom right">You create an array that you only use once (this wastes memory)</li>
<li id=4353 pos="bottom right">This code actually loops over that array twice! :(</li>
<p id=4354 pos="bottom right">Luckily Guido and his team were generous enough to develop generators so we could just do this;</p>
<span id=4357 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">def</span>
<span id=4358 class="hljs-title function_" pos="bottom right">myRangeSmart</span>
<span id=4359 class="hljs-params" pos="bottom right">i</span>
<span id=4360 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">0</span>
<span id=4361 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">while</span>
<span id=4362 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">yield</span>
<span id=4363 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">1</span>
<span id=4364 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">return</span>
<span id=4365 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">for</span>
<span id=4366 class="hljs-keyword" pos="bottom right">in</span>
<span id=4367 class="hljs-number" pos="bottom right">10</span>
<span id=4368 class="hljs-built_in" pos="bottom right">print</span>
<code id=4370 pos="bottom right">next()</code>
<code id=4371 pos="bottom right">next()</code>

<path id=4449 class="SVG_CLASS" pos="bottom right"></path>
<strong id=4453 pos="bottom right">Yield is an object</strong>
<code id=4455 pos="bottom right">return</code>
<strong id=4457 pos="bottom right">a function to return a huge set of values</strong>
<code id=4458 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<code id=4460 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<strong id=4461 pos="bottom right">barrier</strong>
<p id=4463 pos="bottom right">like barrier in the CUDA language, it will not transfer control until it gets
  completed.</p>
<code id=4465 pos="bottom right">yield</code>
<p id=4466 pos="bottom right">Then, every other call will run the loop you have written in the function one more time, returning the next value until there isn't any value to return.</p>
